Spreading Arms and Separating Belly from Thighs in Sujood: The Sunnah Postures for Men and Women
Sunnah actions of sujood: spreading arms and separating belly from thighs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah postures for men and women in sujood and identify the hadith proof that establishes these postures.

Core Idea
Men spread arms and separate belly from thighs in sujood; women contract for modesty.

Sujood is a position of utmost humility, and the Prophet taught us specific postures to enhance that humility. This lesson examines two sunnah actions: men exposing their armpits and keeping the belly away from thighs, while women huddle closely. We will see the hadith evidence and the wisdom behind the gender distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed postures
For men: expose armpits (raise arms) and separate belly from thighs. For women: contract and huddle the body close.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith from Malik ibn Buhaynah states the Prophet spread his arms until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. This forms the basis for the sunnah.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
The Prophet's action makes it a sunnah; the gender variation is based on modesty (satr).
4
Apply to practice
Recognize that these are recommended, not obligatory; neglecting them does not invalidate sujood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٥] (٢٥) ويبدي ضبعيه ويجافي بطنه عن فخذيه
عن مالك ابن بحينة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذا صلى فرج بين يديه حتى يبدو بياض ابطيه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب یبدي ضبعیه و یجاني جنبه في السجود ص ٥٦ نمبر ٨٠٧ر مسلم شریف ، باب الاعتدال في السجود و وضع الكفين على الارض ص ١٩٤ نمبر ٤٩٥) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا كہ بغل كو ران سے اور پیٹ سے اتنا الگ ركھے كه آدمی پیچھے سے اس كی بغل كی سفیدی دیکھ سكے۔
عورت سكڑ کر سجدہ كرے گی۔ یہ اس كے ستر كے لئے بہتر ہے۔
ضبع : ضبع تثنیہ كا صیغہ ہے بغل، یجانی : دور ركھے۔
[15] (25) He exposes his armpits and separates his belly from his thighs. From Malik ibn Buhaynah that the Messenger of Allah, when he prayed, would spread his arms until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that he should keep the armpit so far from the thigh and belly that a person can see the whiteness of his armpit from behind. A woman should contract (huddle) in prostration. This is better for her modesty. (Note: ضبع is the dual form of armpit; يجافي means to keep away.)
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage outlines the sunnah posture for sujood. For men, the command is to expose the armpits (بدي ضبعيه) by raising the arms and keeping them away from the sides, and to separate the belly from the thighs, creating space. The hadith of Malik ibn Buhaynah is presented as proof: the Prophet used to spread his arms so much that the whiteness of his armpits could be seen from behind. For women, the sunnah is the opposite: they should contract and huddle closely to conceal themselves, which is better for their modesty (satr). The final line provides lexical explanation: ضبع (is the dual form) meaning armpits; يجافي means to keep away. This distinction between male and female posture is a distinctive feature of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
إبداء الضبعين (ibda' al-dab'ayn): Exposing the armpits by raising the arms away from the sides during sujood.
يجافي (yujafi): To keep away, to separate (the belly from the thighs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the sunnah posture for a woman in sujood?
A) Spread arms wide
B) Contract and huddle
C) Lift feet
D) Place forehead first

Key Takeaway
Men spread arms and separate belly from thighs in sujood; women contract; both are sunnah based on prophetic practice and modesty considerations.

Directing Toes Towards Qibla in Sujood
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling for directing toes during sujood and cite the hadith evidence from Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi.

Core Idea
Align your toes towards the qibla in sujood – the Prophet's practice shows every part faces the House of Allah.

This lesson addresses a specific sunnah of sujood often overlooked: the direction of the toes. The passage provides a hadith from Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi describing the Prophet's prayer, establishing that even the tips of the feet should face the qibla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is directing the toes of both feet towards the qibla during sujood. Identify the hukm: what is the ruling – fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.?
The passage uses 'yuwajjih' (directs) – a description of the Prophet's action.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi reported by Bukhari. Note that it is a description of the Prophet's prayer.
The hadith is partially quoted in the text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Determine how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit phrase 'faced the qibla with the tips of his toes' directly prescribes the act.
The evidence is from the Prophet's action (fi'l), not a verbal command.
4
Note the status
Classify the ruling: is it sunnah or wajib? The Prophet's consistent action in worship indicates sunnah unless there is evidence of obligation.
Hanafis consider this sunnah, not wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١٦] (٢٦) ويوجه اصابع رجليه نحو القبلة
يستقبل بأطراف رجليه القبلة قال ابو حميد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب يستقبل بأطراف رجليه القبلة ص ١١٢) فقال ابو حميد الساعدي انا كنت احفظكم لصلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر الحديث وفيه واذا سجد وضع يديه غير مفترش ولا قابضهما واستقبل بأطراف اصابع رجليه القبلة (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب سته ...) (الحاشية مقطوعة)
[16] (26) He directs the toes of his feet towards the qibla. He faces the qibla with the tips of his feet. Abu Hamid reported from the Prophet. (Bukhari, Bab: He faces the qibla with the tips of his feet). Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi said: I am the most knowledgeable among you about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, and he mentioned the hadith, and in it: When he prostrated, he placed his hands not spreading nor clamping them, and faced the qibla with the tips of his toes. (Bukhari, Bab... the footnote is cut off.)
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This short passage establishes another sunnah of sujood: the worshipper should direct the toes of both feet towards the qibla. The proof is from the hadith of Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi, who described the Prophet's prayer in detail, stating that when he prostrated, he placed his hands without spreading them out (i.e., keeping fingers together?) and without clamping them to the ground, and he faced the qibla with the tips of his toes. This ruling underscores the importance of aligning all body parts towards the qibla during prayer as a sign of devotion and unity of direction. The hadith reference in the text is partially preserved; the complete hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari.

Key Terms
أطراف الأصابع (atraf al-asabi'): The tips of the toes, which should be pointed toward the qibla during sujood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should be done with the toes during sujood according to this passage?
A) They should be curled under.
B) They should be pointed towards the qibla.
C) They should be flat on the ground.
D) They should be raised off the ground.

Key Takeaway
Directing the toes toward the qibla during sujood is a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him), established by his action.

Prostration on Edge of Turban: Permissibility with Thin Barrier
Ruling with proof on prostrating on turban edge or extra garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prostrating on a thin barrier and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Prostrating on a thin garment edge is valid—the forehead need not directly touch the ground.

This passage presents a key ruling from the matn: it is permissible (jā'iz) to prostrate on the edge of one's turban or excess clothing. The sharh supports it with a hadith of the Companion Anas ibn Mālik, showing that in severe heat the Prophet's Companions would place the edge of their garments on the ground for sajdah. Understanding this ruling clarifies that a thin barrier does not invalidate prostration, which is an important point in the chapter of salāh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that prostrating on the edge of the turban or on extra clothing is permissible (jā'iz). Note the specific terms: 'kawr' (edge) vs. the thick middle, and 'fāḍil' (excess) as in the hem or sleeve.
The ruling applies only to the thin part; the thick middle may prevent valid sajdah.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Anas ibn Mālik reports that during severe heat, the Companions would place the edge of their garment (ṭaraf al-thawb) under their foreheads in sajdah. This is recorded in al-Bukhārī and other collections.
The hadith is an ahad narration, so it is zannī al-thubūt, but accepted in fiqh for practice.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalālah
The phrase 'يضع أحدنا طرف الثوب' indicates that placing the garment's edge is an accepted practice. The reason 'shiddat al-ḥarr' shows that it is permissible even without necessity, as it was done under the Prophet's supervision.
The permissibility is not limited to cases of hardship; it is generally allowed.
4
Note the scope and limitation
The commentary adds a note distinguishing the edge (thin) from the middle (thick). Prostration on the thick part may be invalid because it prevents direct forehead contact.
This indicates that the barrier must be thin; a thick barrier may invalidate the rukn.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Some schools require direct contact of the forehead with the ground without any barrier. The Hanafi position relies on this hadith to allow a thin barrier, while others may argue it contradicts the principle of direct contact.
The practical difference is whether a thin cloth on the prostration spot is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۴] (۲۴) فان سجد على كور عمامته او علی فاضل ثوبه جاز [۱۹۴] (۲۴) اگر پگڑی کے کنارے پر یا زائد کپڑے پر سجدہ کیا تو جائز ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن انس بن مالك قال كنا نصلى مع النبى الله الله فيضع احد نا طرف الثوب من شدة الحر في مكان السجود (الف) ( بخاری شریف باب المجد و علی الثوب في شدة الحرص ۵۶ نمبر ۳۸۵ رنسائی شریف ، باب السجود علی الثياب ص ۱۲۵ نمبر ارابوداؤد شریف ، باب الرجل يسجد علی تو به ص ۱۰۳ نمبر ۶۶۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمامہ کے کنارے پر سجدہ کرنے سے سجدہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ نت کور : عمامہ کا بیچ ، کناره
If he prostrates on the edge of his turban or on the excess of his garment, it is permissible. If one prostrated on the edge of the turban or on extra clothing, it is permissible. There is a hadith: from Anas ibn Malik, he said: We used to pray with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and one of us would place the edge of the garment on the place of prostration due to intense heat. (Bukhari, chapter on prostrating on clothing in severe heat, no. 385; Nasa'i, chapter on prostration on garments; Abu Dawud, chapter on a man prostrating on his garment, no. 660). From this hadith it is understood that prostrating on the edge of the turban makes the prostration valid. Note: the middle of the turban, the edge.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn: it is valid (jā'iz) to prostrate on the edge of one's turban or on an extra piece of clothing. The Urdu commentary clarifies and supports it with a hadith from Anas ibn Malik, showing that in severe heat the Companions would place the edge of their garment under their foreheads. This indicates that a thin barrier is acceptable. The note distinguishes the middle of the turban from the edge, implying the middle is thick and may not suffice.

Key Terms
کور عمامته (kawr 'imāmatihi): The edge or corner of the turban
فاضل ثوبه (fāḍil thawbihī): The excess part of one's garment, such as the hem or sleeve

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on prostrating on the edge of the turban according to the Hanafi school?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Ja'iz (permissible)
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits prostration on the thin edge of a turban or clothing, based on the practice of the Companions.

Spreading Arms in Prostration: Sunna for Men, Modesty for Women
Ruling on recommended posture in prostration with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunna posture for men and women in prostration, cite the hadith proof, and distinguish the rulings between genders.

Core Idea
Men spread arms in prostration; women keep close — the sunna follows modesty.

During prostration, the recommended posture differs between men and women. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ, instructs men to hold their upper arms away from the sides and separate the belly from the thighs, while women are to remain compact. This lesson examines the evidence and practical application of this sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what posture is being prescribed and for whom. The text states that it is sunna for men to spread the arms (reveal armpits) and keep the belly from touching the thighs. For women, the opposite is recommended.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Malik ibn Buhaynah: the Prophet ﷺ would spread his arms in prostration until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. This is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'farraja bayna yadayhi' (spread his arms) and 'hatta yabdu bayad ibtayhi' (until the whiteness of his armpits appeared) indicate the extent of separation. This teaches the recommended posture.
4
Note the gender distinction
The commentary adds that women should prostrate compactly, keeping limbs close together, as it is more modest and concealing.
This distinction is based on the principle that women's modesty takes precedence.
5
Confirm the hukm level
The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not wajib. If a man does not spread his arms, his prayer remains valid but he loses the reward of following this sunna.
This avoids confusion with obligatory acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۹۵] (۲۵) ویبدی ضبعيه ويجافي بطنه عن فخذيه [۱۹۵] (۲۵) دونوں بغلوں کو کشادہ رکھیں اور پیٹ کو رانوں سے الگ رکھے۔ مرد اس طرح سجدہ کرے کہ بغل پیٹ سے دور رہے۔ اور ران بھی پیٹ سے الگ رہے۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے عن مالک ابن بحينة ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذا صلى فرج بين يديه حتى يبدو بياض ابطیه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب یجافی بین یدیہ و یجانی جنبہ فی السجود ص ۵۶ نمبر ۸۰۷، مسلم شریف، باب الاعتدال في السجود و وضع الکفین على الارض ص ۱۹۴ نمبر ۴۹۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بغل کو ران سے اور پیٹ سے اتنا الگ رکھے کہ آدمی پیچھے سے اس کی بغل کی سفیدی دیکھ سکے۔ عورت سکڑ کر سجدہ کرے گی۔ یہ اس کے ستر کے لئے بہتر ہے۔ ات ضبع : ضبع تثنیہ کا صیغہ ہے بغل، یجانی : دور رکھے۔
And he reveals his armpits and separates his belly from his thighs. Keep both armpits open and keep the belly separate from the thighs. A man should prostrate such that his armpits are away from his belly and his thighs are also away from his belly. The proof of this is a hadith from Malik ibn Buhaynah that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed, he spread his arms until the whiteness of his armpits appeared. (Bukhari, chapter on spreading arms in prostration; Muslim). From this hadith it is understood that one should keep his armpits and belly so far apart that a person can see the whiteness of his armpits from behind. A woman should prostrate in a compact position; this is better for her modesty. 'ضبع' is the dual form meaning armpits, 'يجافي' means to keep apart.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage states a sunnah action for men: during prostration, the upper arms should be held away from the sides (showing the armpits), and the belly should not touch the thighs. The hadith from Malik ibn Buhaynah confirms this practice. The commentary adds that for women, the sunnah is the opposite: they should keep their limbs close together for modesty. The terms 'ضبع' and 'يجافي' are explained.

Key Terms
ضبعيه (ḍab'ayhi): His two armpits
يجافي (yujāfī): Keeps apart, separates
فرج بين يديه (farraja bayna yadayhi): He spread his arms/hands
بياض ابطیه (bayāḍ ibṭayhi): Whiteness of his armpits

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a man who prostrates without spreading his arms?
A) His prayer is invalid because he omitted a wajib.
B) His prayer is valid but he misses the reward of the sunnah.
C) His prayer is valid only if he makes sajdah al-sahw.
D) His prayer is invalid because he changed the posture.

Key Takeaway
Men should spread their arms and separate their belly from thighs in prostration (sunnah); women should keep their limbs close for modesty.

Pointing Toes to Qiblah in Prostration
Ruling on the sunnah of pointing toes to the qiblah during sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling for pointing toes during sajdah and explain its evidence from the hadith of Abu Humayd.

Core Idea
Pointing toes to qiblah in sajdah is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib, from the Prophet's practice.

This lesson focuses on a detail of prostration posture: directing the toes towards the qiblah. While often overlooked, the hadith evidence from the Prophet's ﷺ prayer clearly establishes this as a regular practice. Understanding its status as sunnah (not wajib) helps us balance following the sunnah with recognizing its non-obligatory nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the toes should be directed towards the qiblah during prostration. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan al-Bayhaqi. The hadith describes the Prophet's prayer, including that he would face the tips of his toes towards the qiblah when prostrating.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), but it is authentic.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'wa-staqbala bi-atrāfi aṣābi'i rijlayhi l-qiblah' (he faced the tips of his toes towards the qiblah). The word istiqbāl (facing) indicates deliberate direction, and the specific mention of toes shows the exact body part.
No explicit command, but the Prophet's continuous action indicates sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All major schools agree this is recommended. There is no significant dispute on the ruling itself; the difference is in emphasis: some call it mustahabb, Hanafis call it sunnah mu'akkadah.
No school treats it as wajib or fard.
5
Determine mufta bihi
The operative position is that pointing toes to the qiblah is a sunnah. Missing it does not invalidate the prayer, but one loses the reward of following the Prophetic model.
The hadith is strong enough to establish desirability, but not obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۹۶] (۲۶) ويوجه اصابع رجليه نحو القبلة [۱۹۶] (۲۶) سجدہ کی حالت میں دونوں پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف متوجہ رہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے يستقبل بـاطـراف رجليه القبلة قال ابو حميد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب یستقبل باطراف رجلیہ القبلۃ ص۱۱۲) فقال ابو حميد الساعدى انا كنت احفظكم لصلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكر الحديث وفيه واذا سجد وضع يديه غير مفترش ولا قابضهما واستقبل باطراف اصابع رجليه القبلة (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب وضع اليدين في السجود)  ... الجلوس في التشهد ص ۱۴ نمبر ۸۲۸ سنن للبیھقی ، باب نصب قدميه و يستقبل باطراف اصابعهما القبلة ، ج ثانی ،ص ۱۶۷، نمبر ۲۷۱۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ کی حالت میں پاؤں کی انگلیاں قبلہ کی طرف رکھنا چاہئے۔
And he directs the toes of his feet towards the qiblah. During prostration, the toes of both feet should be facing the qiblah. There is a hadith: 'He faces the qiblah with the ends of his feet.' Abu Humayd said from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Al-Bukhari, chapter on facing the qiblah with the ends of the feet. Then Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said: 'I am the one who best preserves among you the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' He mentioned the hadith and in it: 'When he prostrated, he placed his hands neither spread nor tucked, and he faced the qiblah with the tips of his toes.' (Bukhari). And the hadith about sitting in tashahhud, etc. From this hadith it is understood that one should place the toes towards the qiblah during prostration.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that the toes should face the qiblah during prostration. The hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi describes the Prophet's prayer in detail, including that he faced his toes toward the qiblah. The commentary advises that this is a sunnah action. The additional reference from Bayhaqi emphasizes the same point.

Key Terms
اصابع رجليه (aṣābi' rijlayhi): The toes of his feet

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on pointing the toes towards the qiblah during prostration?
A) Fard – omission invalidates prayer
B) Wajib – omission requires sajdah sahw
C) Sunnah – recommended, omission no penalty
D) Mubah – optional, no reward

Key Takeaway
Pointing the toes towards the qiblah during prostration is a confirmed sunnah, not a fard or wajib, based on the Prophet's practice preserved in authentic hadith.

The Tasbih in Prostration: Minimum Three Times, a Sunnah
Ruling on the tasbih in prostration: minimum three times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the tasbih in prostration, identify its sunnah status, and distinguish it from the fard of sajdah.

Core Idea
The tasbih in prostration is sunnah; three times is the minimum, but the fard is only placing the forehead.

In this lesson, we examine the wording of the prostration tasbih as taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The passage from our text presents the minimum number of recitations and clarifies the legal status of this act. We will look at the hadith evidence and understand how Hanafi fiqh classifies the tasbih as sunnah while emphasizing that the obligatory element of sajdah is simply the placement of the forehead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' in prostration. The ruling is that it is sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud is cited.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni evidence.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'فقد تم سجوده' indicates completion with three tasbihs, and 'ذلك أدناه' sets the minimum.
The word 'تم' means 'is complete', not 'is obligatory'.
4
Distinguish between fard and sunnah
The commentary clarifies that the fard is only placing the forehead; the tasbih is part of the sunnah.
The fard of sajdah is a rukn; the tasbih is a mustahabb (sunnah) act.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools consider it wajib; Hanafis maintain it is sunnah.
The difference is based on the interpretation of 'تم'.

And he says in his prostration: 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times, and that is the minimum. In prostration, say 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' three times, and this is the lowest level. From Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When he prostrates and says in his prostration Subhana Rabbi al-A'la three times, his prostration is complete, and that is the minimum.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that one should say Subhana Rabbi al-A'la three times, and this is the minimum; if one says more, it is better. The obligatory part of prostration is fulfilled by merely placing the forehead on the ground; the rest are sunnan.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage states that the sunnah tasbih in prostration is to say 'Subhana Rabbi al-A'la' at least three times. The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud confirms that three times completes the prostration, indicating that saying less is not considered complete. However, the commentary clarifies that the fard (obligatory) part of sajdah is only the placement of the forehead; the tasbih and other actions are sunnah. Therefore, if one omits the tasbih, the prostration is still valid but deficient.

Raising the Head from Prostration with Takbir and the Sitting of Tranquility
Ruling with proof on raising head and sitting between prostrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising the head from prostration and the sitting of tranquility, and explain the dispute over whether ta'dil al-arkan is wajib or sunnah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's long pause between prostrations shows the importance of tranquility, but whether it is wajib or sunnah is a debated point.

In this lesson, we examine the sunnah of raising the head from prostration while saying takbir and sitting with tranquility. We study the hadith from Anas that demonstrates the Prophet's practice and consider the scholarly dispute over the legal status of this posture balance. The passage also clarifies a boundary condition: if one raises the head enough to nearly sit, the prostration is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn says 'then he raises his head and says takbir'. The commentator adds that one should sit with complete tranquility. In the Hanafi school, this act is considered sunnah (recommended).
The ruling here is sunnah, but the text soon notes an ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim via Anas ibn Malik: the Prophet would sit between the two prostrations until people thought he had forgotten.
The hadith is a dalil naqli (textual proof) of the Prophet's practice.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'until we thought he had forgotten' indicates a significant pause. Some jurists take this long pause as evidence that tranquility (tuma'ninah) is wajib (necessary).
Hanafis generally see it as sunnah because the Prophet's action is not accompanied by a command.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf
Some imams (possibly within or outside Hanafi) consider ta'dil al-arkan (proper posture balance) as wajib due to this hadith. The practical difference is that if wajib, omitting requires sajdah al-sahw; if sunnah, no compensation.
The thamarah al-khilaf directly affects the validity and corrective measures in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۹۸] (۲۸) ثم يرفع رأسه ويكبر [۱۹۸] (۲۸) پھر سر اٹھائے اور تکبیر کہے۔ تکبیر کہتے ہوئے جلسہ میں پورے اطمینان سے بیٹھے۔ انس ... كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا قال سمع لمن حمده قام حتى نقول قد اوهم ثم يسجد و يقعد بين السجدتين حتى نقول قد اوهم (ب) (مسلم شریف ، باب اعتدال ارکان الصلوة وتخفیفها تمام ص ۱۸۹ نمبر ۴۷۳) یعنی آپ دونوں سجدوں کے درمیان اتنی دیر تک بیٹھتے کہ لوگوں کو خیال ہوتا کہ شاید آپ بھول گئے ہیں۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قومہ میں اطمینان سے بیٹھنا چاہئے ۔ ان ہی احادیث کی وجہ سے بعض ائمہ کے نزدیک تعدیل ارکان واجب ہے۔ اتنا سر اٹھایا کہ بیٹھنے کے قریب ہو گیا تو پہلا سجدہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔
Then he raises his head and says takbir. Then raise the head and say takbir. While saying takbir, sit in complete tranquility in the sitting position. Anas narrated: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah,' he would stand until we thought he had forgotten, then he would prostrate and sit between the two prostrations until we thought he had forgotten. (Muslim). That is, he would sit between the two prostrations for such a long time that people thought he might have forgotten. From this it is understood that one should sit with tranquility in the sitting (between prostrations). Because of these hadiths, some imams consider the proper observance of postures (ta'dil al-arkan) as wajib. If one raised his head so much that he came close to sitting, his first prostration is valid.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage covers the sunnah of raising the head from prostration while saying the takbir, and then sitting with tranquility (jalsah) between the two prostrations. The hadith from Anas shows that the Prophet would pause a long time between prostrations, indicating the importance of tranquility. The commentator notes that some imams consider this moderation of postures (ta'dil al-arkan) as wajib, implying that in their view it is necessary to pause sufficiently. The final line clarifies that if one raises the head enough to nearly sit, the first prostration is valid.

Key Terms

The Prophet's long pause between prostrations underscores the importance of tranquility, but whether that makes it wajib or sunnah is a point of internal Hanafi debate.

Sitting with Tranquility Before Second Prostration
Ruling on the second prostration after sitting with tranquility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tranquility before the second prostration and identify the proof from the hadith of the man who prayed incorrectly.

Core Idea
Tranquility before the second prostration is a sunnah affirmed by the Prophet's teaching to the man who prayed incorrectly.

In this lesson, we examine the specific moment between the first and second prostrations. The source text instructs that after sitting up from the first prostration, one must pause until tranquil before proceeding to the second. We will explore the ruling and the evidence from the famous hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sequence
The act described is the transition from the sitting after the first prostration to the second prostration. The key element is tranquility (itmi'nān) in the sitting before the takbir and second sajdah.
The sitting itself (jalsah) is a wajib in Hanafi; the tranquility is a sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of the man who prayed incorrectly (Sahih al-Bukhari). The Prophet instructed him: '...then prostrate until you are tranquil in prostration, then raise until you are tranquil while sitting, then prostrate until you are tranquil in prostration.'
This hadith is ahad (single-narrator) but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Note the Hanafi hukm level
In the Hanafi school, tranquility (tuma'ninah) in each posture is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard or wajib. The prostration itself is a rukn (fard), and the sitting (jalsah) is wajib.
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider tuma'ninah wajib in all postures.
4
Cross-madhhab note
The requirement of tranquility is a point of ikhtilaf. Hanafis rely on the apparent command 'حتى تطمئن' but interpret it as a guidance to completeness (sunnah), not an obligation.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if one rushes without tranquility, the prayer is still valid in Hanafi but deficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۹۹] (۲۹) واذا اطمئن جالسا كبر و سجد [۱۹۹] (۲۹) اور جب اطمینان سے بیٹھ جائے تو تکبیر کہے اور سجدہ کرے۔ دوسرے سجدے کی دلیل بہت سی احادیث میں ہے مثلا عن ابي هريرة ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم دخل المسجد فدخل رجل فصلى ... ثم اسجد حتى تطمئن ساجدا ثم ارفع حتى تطمئن جالسائم اسجد حتى تطمئن ساجدا ثم افعل ذلك في صلوتک كلها (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب امر النبي الذي لا يتم رکوعہ بالاعادة ص ۱۰۹ نمبر ۷۹۳) اس حدیث میں غلطی کرنے والے کو تعلیم دی گئی ہے۔
And when he is tranquil while sitting, he says takbir and prostrates. And when he is convinced and sitting with tranquility, he says takbir and prostrates. The proof of the second prostration is found in many hadiths, for example from Abu Hurairah: The Prophet (peace be upon him) entered the mosque, and a man entered and prayed... then prostrate until you are tranquil in prostration, then raise until you are tranquil while sitting, then prostrate until you are tranquil in prostration, then do that in all your prayer. (Bukhari). In this hadith, the one who made a mistake is taught.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage instructs that after the first prostration and the sitting, one should say takbir and perform the second prostration with tranquility. The hadith from Abu Hurairah is the 'Hadith of the Man Who Prayed Incorrectly,' where the Prophet taught him to pause in each position, including the second prostration. This emphasizes that tranquility (itmi'nan) is essential for every posture.

Key Terms
اطمئنان (iṭmi'nān): Tranquility, calmness, pausing until every limb is settled.
جلسة (jalsah): The sitting between the two prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Recite more tasbih

Key Takeaway
Sitting with tranquility before the second prostration is a sunnah established by the hadith of the man who prayed incorrectly.

The Ruling on Sitting Between Sujuds and the Second Prostration
Rulings on raising head, sitting calmly, and performing second sujud with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsah) and the second prostration, cite the relevant hadith evidence, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Sitting calmly between prostrations is wajib; the second prostration is fard.

Having risen from the first sajdah, the worshiper must now pause with calmness before the second. This lesson examines the rulings on this sitting (jalsah) and the second sujud, based on the hadith of Anas and Abu Hurairah. The Hanafi school holds that tadil al-arkan (performing each posture with calmness) is wajib, a position supported by the Prophet's lengthy pauses and the explicit command in the hadith of the man who prayed badly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Determine which actions are mentioned: raising the head with takbir, sitting calmly between the two prostrations, and the second prostration. Classify each according to Hanafi: the sitting calmly is wajib, the second prostration is fard.
The matn numbers (28) and (29) indicate these are separate elements.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites two hadiths: one from Anas (Muslim) showing the Prophet's long sitting, and one from Abu Hurairah (Bukhari) where the Prophet commands calmness in sujud and jalsah. Identify these as ahad hadith.
Both hadiths are zanni al-thubut but widely accepted.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's constant practice (in the Anas hadith) indicates wujub according to Hanafi usul. The command 'until you are calm' in the Abu Hurairah hadith implies obligation because al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
The Shafi'i school interprets these as recommended (sunnah), not obligatory.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i considers tadil al-arkan as sunnah. Their evidence: the same hadiths but with a different usul principle – they hold that the Prophet's actions do not always indicate obligation unless there is a command.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf in usul.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school gives weight to the explicit command and the fact that the Prophet consistently performed these actions with emphasis. Therefore, the mufta bihi position is that tadil al-arkan is wajib, and its omission requires sajdah sahw.
The second sujud itself is fard; if omitted, the prayer is invalid.

The Hanafi position: sitting calmly between sujuds is wajib (for tadil), and the second sujud is fard.

Standing from Sujud and Jalsat al-Istirahah
Ruling on standing from sujud and inter-madhhab dispute on jalsat al-istirahah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jalsat al-istirahah, identify the Shafi'i proof, and explain the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Jalsat al-istirahah is permissible but not sunnah; the Prophet's sitting was due to old age.

When standing from the second prostration, the Hanafi school teaches a specific method: rise on the upper part of the feet, support on the knees, and do not sit briefly. Yet there is a well-known dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding this brief sitting called jalsat al-istirahah. In this lesson, we will examine the Hanafi ruling, the Shafi'i proof, and the Hanafi response based on the hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the precise Hanafi position: one should stand directly from sujud without sitting (jalsat al-istirahah). The text also forbids leaning on hands.
The ruling is based on hadith from Abu Hurairah and Muhammad ibn Hajada.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that jalsat al-istirahah is sunnah after the second sajdah before standing, especially in odd-numbered rak'ahs.
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's sitting was due to old age, not a regular sunnah. However, if someone does it, no sajdat al-sahw is required.
The response respects the hadith but limits its application to a specific situation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis consider jalsat al-istirahah mubah (permissible) but not sunnah; Shafi'is consider it sunnah. This affects whether one is rewarded for doing it or considered deficient for leaving it.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that it is permissible but not recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۰) فاذا اطمئن ساجدا كبر واستوى قائما على صدور قدميه ولا يقعد ولا يعتمد بيديه على الارض. [۲۰] (۳۱) ويفعل فى الركعة الثانية مثل ما فعل فى الاولى والے صحابی کو دوسرا سجدہ کرنے کی بھی تلقین کی ہے۔ اس لئے دوسرا سجدہ بھی فرض ہے جس طرح پہلا سجدہ فرض ہے۔ (۲۰۰) (۳۰) پس جب اطمینان سے سجدہ کرلے تو تکبیر کہے اور دونوں قدموں کے سینے کے بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے ۔ اور بیٹھے نہیں اور نہ دونوں ہاتھوں سے زمین کا سہارا لے۔ تفریق سجدہ سے کھڑے ہوتے وقت درمیان میں جلسہ استراحت نہ کرے اور نہ زمین کا سہارا لے کر کھڑا ہو بلکہ دونوں ہاتھوں سے گھٹنے کا سہارا لے اور سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے۔

۔

(30) When he is calm in prostration, he says takbir and stands straight on the upper part of his feet, and he does not sit and does not support himself with his hands on the ground. After the prostration, when standing, he does not do jalsat al-istiraha in between, nor does he stand by leaning on the ground, but supports himself with both hands on the knees and stands straight. There is a hadith from Abu Hurairah: The Prophet used to rise in prayer on the upper part of his feet. (Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi). From this we know that he did not sit but stood on his feet. (2) From Muhammad ibn Hajada: When he stood, he stood on his knees and supported himself on his thighs. (Abu Dawud). From this too we know that he stood straight. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, there is a jalsat al-istiraha (sitting of rest) after the final prostration. His proof is the hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith: He saw the Prophet praying, and when he was in an odd rakah, he would not rise until he was sitting straight. (Bukhari, Tirmidhi). And also: When he raised his head from the second prostration, he sat and leaned on the ground then stood. (Bukhari). From this hadith it is known that jalsat al-istiraha is sunnah. Our response is that this was done due to old age. However, if someone does jalsat al-istiraha, he does not have to perform sajdat al-sahw because it is established by hadith. Note: 'Sudur qadamayh' means the upper part of the foot on which a person stands.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage begins with the ruling on standing from the second sujud. The text prohibits sitting (jalsat al-istirahah) and leaning on hands. The commentary provides two hadiths: one from Abu Hurairah about standing on the feet, and one from Muhammad ibn Hajada about supporting on knees. Then a benefit (fa'idah) discusses the Shafi'i position on jalsat al-istirahah (sitting briefly before standing). The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the Prophet did that due to old age, but it is not required. However, if one does it, no sajdat al-sahw is needed. The passage concludes with a definition of 'sudur qadamayh'. This is a clear inter-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
جلسة استراحة (jalsat al-istirahah): A brief sitting after the second prostration before standing up for the next rak'ah
صدور قدمیہ (sudur qadamayh): The upper part of the feet, upon which one stands

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Due to old age
C) To teach a ruling
D) It was abrogated

Key Takeaway
Jalsat al-istirahah is permissible (mubah) in Hanafi fiqh but not sunnah; the sunnah is to stand directly from sujud.

Differences in the Second Rak'ah: Thana and Ta'awwudh
Ruling stating that second rak'ah is like first except no thana or ta'awwudh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two elements omitted in the second rak'ah and explain why they are not repeated.

Core Idea
Thana and ta'awwudh are sunnah only in the first rak'ah; the second rak'ah repeats all other actions.

The second rak'ah of every salat follows the same structure as the first, except for two opening acts: the thana (praise) and ta'awwudh (seeking refuge). This lesson clarifies this rule and its wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its parts
The passage discusses the second rak'ah of salat. Identify that it is a single unit of prayer.
Focus on the two specific omissions.
2
Recognize what is omitted
The text says thana and ta'awwudh are not recited in the second rak'ah. Memorize these two terms.
They are opening supplications.
3
Understand the reason
Both are sunnah only for the beginning of the prayer. The first rak'ah serves as the opening, so they are not needed later.
This applies to all prayers with multiple rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۰۱] (۳۱) ويفعل فى الركعة الثانية مثل ما فعل فى الاولى مگر یہ کہ مثانہ پڑھے اور اعوذ باللہ نہ پڑھے۔ نا صرف پہلی رکعت میں پڑھی جاتی ہے۔ اسی طرح اعوذ باللہ بھی پہلی رکعت میں پڑھی جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے دوسری رکعت میں یہ دونوں نہ پڑھے۔
(31) He does in the second rak'ah the same as he did in the first, except that he does not recite thana and does not recite ta'awwudh. Thana is recited only in the first rak'ah. Similarly, ta'awwudh is recited only in the first rak'ah. Therefore, in the second rak'ah, he does not recite these two.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling statement. It clarifies that the second rak'ah follows the same pattern as the first except for two omissions: the thana (opening supplication) and the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) are not repeated. They are exclusively for the first rak'ah. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening praise recited after takbirat al-ihram
اعوذ بالله (ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' recited before fatiha

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Thana and ta'awwudh are exclusively recited in the first rak'ah of every salat.

Standing from Prostration: No Sitting or Leaning on Hands
Ruling on standing from prostration with proof and refutation of jalsa istiraahat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing from prostration, cite the two primary hadith proofs, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position on jalsa istiraahat.

Core Idea
Stand directly on the tops of your feet — no sitting, no hand support on the ground.

In the Hanafi prayer, every movement has a prescribed manner. This lesson examines a specific point: how to rise from prostration. The text provides the ruling along with its proofs and refutes the practice of sitting briefly before standing (jalsa istiraahat). Understanding this difference will clarify both the Hanafi method and the basis for the ikhtilaf with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: the worshipper stands on the tops of the feet without sitting and without supporting himself with hands on the ground.
The author also permits using hands on knees for support.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the two hadith cited: from Abu Huraira (rising on tops of feet) and from Muhammad ibn Hajada (rising on knees, leaning on thighs).
Both are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut) but considered qat'i al-dalala for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Examine the Arabic phrases: 'yanhadu 'an sudur qadamayhi' indicates direct rising; 'nahada 'ala rukbatayhi wa i'tamada 'ala fakhidhayhi' shows standing on knees/thighs, not sitting.
The absence of any mention of sitting is the key proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing Shafi'i view: jalsa istiraahat is sunnah, especially in odd rak'ahs. Their evidence: hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith describing the Prophet sitting and leaning on the ground.
The Hanafi response: that action was due to the Prophet's old age, not a general sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. The Prophet's later practice (direct rising) is taken as the normative sunnah. However, performing jalsa istiraahat does not require sajdah sahw because it is also supported by some narrations.
This concession shows the school's internal consistency: the practice is not required but not sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا اطمئن ساجدا كبر واستوى قائما على صدور قدميه ولا يقعد ولا يعتمد بيديه على الارض. پس جب اطمینان سے سجدہ کرلے تو تکبیر کہے اور دونوں قدموں کے سینے کے بل سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے ۔ اور بیٹھے نہیں اور نہ دونوں ہاتھوں سے زمین کا سہارا لے۔ تفریق سجدہ سے کھڑے ہوتے وقت درمیان میں جلسہ استراحت نہ کرے اور نہ زمین کا سہارا لے کر کھڑا ہو بلکہ دونوں ہاتھوں سے گھٹنے کا سہارا لے اور سیدھا کھڑا ہو جائے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة قال كان النبي الله ينهض فى الصلوة عن صدور قدمیه (الف) ( ترمذی شریف، باب منه اليضا ( كيف الحوض من السجود ( ص ۶۴ نمبر ۲۸۸ سفن بیھقی ، باب من قال پر جمع علی صدور قدمیہ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۷۹، نمبر ۲۷۶۳) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ بیٹھتے نہیں بلکہ پاؤں کے بل کھڑے ہو جاتے (۲) عن محمد بن حجادة اذا نهض على ركبتيه واعتمد على فخذيه (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب افتتاح الصلوۃ ص ۱۴ نمبر ۷۳۶) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ سیدھے کھڑے ہو جاتے تھے۔ فائدہ امام شافعی کے یہاں سجدہ اخیرہ کے بعد جلسہ استراحت ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے اخبرنی مالک بن الحويرث اللیثی انه رأى النبي الله يصلى فاذا كان في وتر من صلوته لم ينهض حتى يستوى قاعدا (ج) ( بخاری شریف من استوی قاعدا فی و تر من صلوته ثم نصف ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۸۲۳ / ترمذی شریف ، باب کیف النهوض من السجود ص ۶۴ نمبر ۷ (۲۸) (۲) جاء نا مالک بن الحویرث ... واذا رفع رأسه عن ا السجدة الثانية جلس واعتمد على الارض ثم قام ( و ) ( بخاری شریف ، باب کیف يعتمد على الارض اذا قام من الرکعۃ ص ۱۴ نمبر ۸۲۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جلسہ استراحت سنت ہے ۔ ہمارا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ بڑھاپے کے وقت کیا ہے۔ تاہم کوئی جلسہ استراحت کرے گا تو سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ احادیث سے ثابت ہے۔ حاشیہ : ( پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) پھر سجدہ کرو یہاں تک کہ اطمینان سے سجدہ کرو۔ پھر ایسا ہی تمام نمازوں میں کرو (الف) آپ نماز میں کھڑے ہوتے دونوں قدموں کے سینے پر ( یعنی سیدھے کھڑے ہو جاتے ) ( ب ) محمد بن حجادہ سے روایت ہے کہ آپ جب کھڑے ہوتے تو دونوں گھٹنوں کے بل کھڑے ہوتے اور دونوں رانوں پر ٹیک لگاتے (ج) آپ کو دیکھا کہ جب نماز کی طاق رکعت ہوتی تو نہیں کھڑے ہوتے یہاں تک کہ ٹھیک سے بیٹھ جاتے (و) جب دوسرے سجدے سے سر اٹھاتے تو بیٹھ جاتے اور زمین پر ٹیک لگاتے پھر کھڑے ہوتے۔
When he is at ease in prostration, he says the takbir and stands upright on the tops of his feet, and does not sit, and does not support himself with his hands on the ground. So when he completes the prostration with tranquility, he says the takbir and stands straight on the soles of both feet. He does not sit, and he does not take support from the ground with his hands. When rising from prostration, he does not perform the sitting of rest (jalsa istiraahat), nor does he stand by leaning on the ground, but rather he takes support from his knees with his hands and stands straight. There is a hadith from Abu Huraira: "The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to rise in prayer on the tops of his feet." (Tirmidhi, Bab kayfa al-nuhood min al-sujud, p. 64 no. 288; Sunan Bayhaqi, Bab man qala yajma' 'ala sudur qadamayhi, vol. 2, p. 179, no. 2763). From this it is understood that he did not sit but stood on his feet. (2) From Muhammad ibn Hajada: "When he rose, he would rise on his knees and lean on his thighs." (Abu Dawud, Bab iftitah al-salah, p. 14 no. 736). From this hadith it is also understood that he used to stand straight. Benefit: According to Imam Shafi'i, after the final prostration there is a sitting of rest (jalsa istiraahat). His evidence is this hadith: Malik ibn al-Huwayrith al-Laythi informed me that he saw the Prophet (peace be upon him) praying, and when he was in an odd rak'ah of his prayer, he did not rise until he had sat up straight. (Bukhari, Bab man istawa qa'idan fi watr min salatihi thumma nashafa, p. 113 no. 823; Tirmidhi, Bab kayfa al-nuhood min al-sujud, p. 64 no. 7 (28); (2) and when he raised his head from the second prostration, he sat and leaned on the ground, then stood. (Bukhari, Bab kayfa ya'tamidu 'ala al-ard idha qama min al-rak'ah, p. 14 no. 824). From this hadith it is understood that jalsa istiraahat is sunnah. Our response is that this was done at the time of old age. Nevertheless, if someone does the jalsa istiraahat, sajdah sahw will not be necessary because it is proven by hadith. Footnote: (From previous page onwards) Then prostrate until you are at ease in prostration. Then do similarly in all your prayers. (A) He used to stand in prayer on the tops of his feet (i.e., stand straight). (B) From Muhammad ibn Hajada: When he stood, he stood on both knees and leaned on both thighs. (C) He saw that when it was an odd rak'ah of his prayer, he would not stand until he had sat properly. (W) When he raised his head from the second prostration, he sat and leaned on the ground, then stood.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) on the manner of standing from prostration in Hanafi prayer. The author states the ruling: the worshipper, after completing the prostration with tranquility (itminan), should stand straight on the tops of his feet, without sitting (i.e., without the jalsa istiraahat) and without supporting himself with his hands on the ground. Instead, he should use his hands on his knees for support. The author then provides evidence from two hadith: the first from Abu Huraira reports that the Prophet ﷺ used to rise on the tops of his feet, implying no intermediate sitting; the second from Muhammad ibn Hajada indicates rising on the knees with support from the thighs. The passage then addresses the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who considers jalsa istiraahat (a brief sitting between prostration and standing) as sunnah, especially in odd rak'ahs. His evidence is the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith, which describes the Prophet sitting and leaning on the ground before standing. The author gives the Hanafi response: that action was due to the Prophet's old age, not a general sunnah. However, if someone performs jalsa istiraahat, it does not invalidate the prayer and sajdah sahw is not required because the practice is supported by some hadith. The footnote further clarifies that the general instruction is to prostrate with tranquility and then stand, and the various narrations are reconciled by attributing the sitting to old age.

Key Terms
جلسة استراحة (jalsa istiraahat): A brief sitting after prostration before standing, considered sunnah by Shafi'i but not in Hanafi school.
صدور قدميه (sudur qadamayhi): The tops/upper parts of the feet; the balls of the feet on which one stands.
سجدة سہو (sajdah sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct way to stand from prostration?
A) Sit briefly (jalsa istiraahat) then stand.
B) Stand directly on the tops of the feet without sitting.
C) Stand by pushing up with hands on the ground.
D) Roll onto the side then stand.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches to stand directly from prostration without sitting or leaning on hands, and this is supported by explicit hadith; the alternative sitting is attributed to the Prophet's old age and does not invalidate the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Second Rak'ah: Same as First Except No Istiftaah or Ta'awwudh
Ruling on the specific actions of the second rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exceptions in the second rak'ah and correctly apply the rule regarding basmalah in every rak'ah.

Core Idea
In the second rak'ah, the opening supplication and refuge-seeking are omitted; basmalah remains sunnah in every rak'ah.

This lesson examines a foundational rule from the Hanafi school regarding the structure of the salah. The text establishes that the second rak'ah is a mirror of the first, with specific omissions. Understanding this precision helps avoid common mistakes and ensures the prayer is performed as legislated.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the general rule
The worshipper repeats all actions of the first rak'ah in the second. This includes standing, recitation (Fatihah + surah), ruku', sujood, etc.
The baseline is sameness; deviations are explicitly stated.
2
Identify the exceptions
The text explicitly says 'except that he does not recite the opening supplication (istiftaah) and does not seek refuge (ta'awwudh)'. These two acts are only performed in the first rak'ah.
The ta'awwudh is 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim'.
3
Note the continuation of basmalah
The Urdu commentary clarifies that Basmalah is recited quietly before Fatihah in every rak'ah, including the second. A hadith from Ibn Abbas supports this practice.
Basmalah is a sunnah act and is part of the recitation preparation.
4
Understand the hukm level
Istiftaah and ta'awwudh are sunnah muakkadah in the first rak'ah. Omitting them in the second is the established practice; if one recites them in the second, the prayer is still valid, but it is contrary to the sunnah.
This distinction helps in knowing where to offer sujood al-sahw if needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفعل فى الركعة الثانية مثل ما فعل في الاولى الا انه لا يستفتح ولا يتعوذ [۲۰] (٣٢) ولا يرفع يديه الا فى التكبيرة الاولى [٢٠٣] (۳۳) فاذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية في الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى فجلس دوسری رکعت میں بسم اللہ آہستہ سے پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ قرآت سے پہلے بسم اللہ آہستہ سے پڑھنا مسنون ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي الله يفتتح صلوته ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (ترمذی شریف، باب من رأی الجهر بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ص نمبر ۲۴۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر رکعت کو بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم سے شروع کرنا چاہئے (دار قطنی نمبر ۱۴۳ میں بھی ہے)
And he does in the second rak'ah the same as he did in the first, except that he does not recite the opening supplication (istiftaah) and does not seek refuge (ta'awwudh). [20] (32) He does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. [203] (33) When he raises his head from the second prostration in the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits. In the second rak'ah, he will recite Bismillah quietly, because reciting Bismillah before the recitation quietly is sunnah. There is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to open his prayer with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim.' (Tirmidhi, Bab man ra'a al-jahr bi Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, p. no. 245). From this it is understood that every rak'ah should be started with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim (also in Dar Qutni no. 143).

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: in the second rak'ah, the worshipper performs all the actions of the first rak'ah (such as recitation, ruku', sujood) with two exceptions: he does not recite the opening supplication (istiftaah) and does not recite the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge in Allah from Shaytan). These are only done in the first rak'ah. Additionally, the author notes that in the second rak'ah, one should recite the basmalah (Bismillah) quietly before the Fatihah, as it is sunnah to recite it quietly in every rak'ah. A hadith from Ibn Abbas confirms that the Prophet used to begin his prayer with Bismillah. The passage also includes a brief note on the raising of hands and the sitting position, which are part of subsequent masaa'il but are included here due to the page layout.

Key Terms
استفتاح (istiftaah): The opening supplication (e.g., 'Subhanakallahumma wa bihamdika...') recited after the first takbir.
تعوذ (ta'awwudh): The phrase 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' recited before Quran recitation.
بسم الله (basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' recited before Quran recitation in prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Raising Hands Only in the First Takbir: Hanafi Evidence and Dispute with Shafi'is
Ruling on raf' al-yadayn with hadith evidence and refutation of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raf' al-yadayn and distinguish the evidence used by Hanafis and Shafi'is for raising hands in prayer.

Core Idea
Hanafis limit hand-raising to the first takbir to preserve tranquility in prayer.

This lesson examines a foundational difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: when should a worshipper raise his hands during prayer? The Hanafi position, based on hadith commanding stillness and the practice of the early caliphs, restricts raf' al-yadayn to the opening takbir. Understanding the evidence and the principle of tranquility is key to grasping this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify that hands are raised only at the first takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) and not at any other point, such as when bowing or standing for the second rak'ah.
The text opens with 'ولا يرفع يديه الا فى التكبيرة الاولى'.
2
Examine the Hanafi hadith evidence
Analyze the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah (command to be still) and the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (showing the Prophet and caliphs raised hands only at first takbir). Note the chain and implications.
These two hadith form the primary dalil: one prohibits excessive movements, the other reports the limited practice.
3
Identify the tranquility principle
Understand that the command 'be still' (اسكنوا) establishes sukun (tranquility) as a required quality in prayer, which would be disrupted by repeated hand-raising.
This principle (sukun) is used to override any general practice of raising hands.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i evidence
Read the hadith of Ibn 'Umar through Nafi' that he raised hands when standing for the second rak'ah, attributed to the Prophet. Understand why this is presented as a counter-evidence.
The Shafi'i school uses this as a proof for raf' al-yadayn at the start of the second rak'ah.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Realize the practical consequence: Hanafis raise hands only once; Shafi'is raise them multiple times, including at the beginning of the second rak'ah. This affects congregational prayer behind an imam of a different madhhab.
The ruling difference has real-world implications for followers of each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يرفع يديه الا فى التكبيرة الاولى. حنفیہ کے نزدیک تکبیر اولی کے علاوہ میں ہاتھ اٹھانا مسنون نہیں ہے۔ نہ رکوع سے اٹھتے وقت اور نہ دوسری رکعت شروع کرتے وقت ۔ اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر 1 میں نوٹ کے تحت گزر چکی ہے۔ دلیل یہ بھی یادر کھیں کہ کہ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن سمرة قال خرج علينا رسول الله الا الله فقال مالی اراکم رفعی ایدیکم كانها اذ ناب خیل شمس؟ اسكنوا في الصلوة (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب الامر بالسكون في الصلوة وانهى عن الاشارة بالید ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں سکون اور اطمینان مطلوب ہے۔ اور بار بار ہاتھ اٹھانے میں سکون نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی رفع یدین نہیں ہونا چاہئے (۲) عـن عـلـقـمـة عـن عبد الله قال صليت مع النبي الله ومع ابي بكر و مع عمر فلم يرفع ايديهم الا عند التكبيرة الأولى في افتتاح الصلوة (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب ذكر التكبير ورفع الیدین الخ ص ۲۹۶ نمبر ۱۲۰ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء ان النبی ل لم يرفع الا في اول مرة ص ۵۰ نمبر ۲۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر اولی کے علاوہ کسی وقت بھی رفع یدین نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔ قائی امام شافعی دوسری رکعت کے شروع میں بھی رفع یدین کے قائل ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عـن نـافـع ان ابن عمر كان اذا دخل في الصلوة ... واذا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه و رفع ذلك ابن عمر الى النبي الله (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب رفع الیدین اذا قام من الرکعتین ص ۱۰۲) اس لئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک دوسری رکعت شروع کرتے وقت بھی رفع یدین ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) جابر بن سمرۃ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور ہمارے سامنے آئے اور فرمایا کہ کیا بات ہے کہ اپنے ہاتھوں کو اٹھائے ہوئے ہوں ۔ گویا کہ دوڑنے والے گھوڑے کی دم ہوں۔ نماز میں سکون سے رہو (ب) فرمایا میں نے نماز پڑھی نبی اور حضرت ابو بکر اور حضرت عمر کے ساتھ ، پس انہوں نے ہاتھ نہیں اٹھائے مگر صرف تکبیر اولی کے وقت نماز کے شروع میں (ج) ابن عمر جب نماز میں داخل ہوتے ... جب دونوں رکعتوں سے کھڑے ہوتے تو ہاتھ اٹھاتے ۔ ابن عمر نے اس حدیث کو حضور تیک مرفوع کیا
He does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. According to the Hanafis, raising hands is not sunnah except at the first takbir – neither when rising from ruku nor when starting the second rak'ah. The evidence for this has already passed in the footnote of mas'alah no. 1. Also remember this hadith: Jabir ibn Samurah said, "The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out to us and said, 'Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be still in prayer.'" (Muslim, Bab al-amr bi al-sukun fi al-salah wa al-nahy 'an al-isharah bi al-yad, p. 181 no. 430). From this hadith it is understood that tranquility and calmness are required in prayer, and repeatedly raising hands disrupts tranquility – therefore raf' al-yadayn should not be done. (2) From 'Alqamah from 'Abdullah, he said: "I prayed with the Prophet (peace be upon him), with Abu Bakr, and with 'Umar, and they did not raise their hands except at the first takbir at the opening of the prayer." (Dar Qutni, Bab dhikr al-takbir wa raf' al-yadayn, p. 296 no. 120; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a anna al-nabi lam yarfa' illa fi awwal marrah, p. 50 no. 257). From this hadith it is understood that raf' al-yadayn should not be done at any time except the first takbir. However, Imam Shafi'i holds that one should raise hands at the beginning of the second rak'ah as well. His evidence is the hadith of Nafi': 'Ibn 'Umar, when he entered the prayer... and when he stood from the two rak'ahs, he raised his hands, and Ibn 'Umar attributed that to the Prophet (peace be upon him).' (Bukhari, Bab raf' al-yadayn idha qama min al-rak'atayn, p. 102). Therefore, according to Imam Shafi'i, there is raf' al-yadayn when starting the second rak'ah. Footnote: (A) Jabir ibn Samurah says: The Prophet came out to us and said, "What is the matter that I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be still in prayer." (B) He said: I prayed with the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar, and they did not raise their hands except at the first takbir at the beginning of the prayer. (C) Ibn 'Umar, when he entered the prayer... and when he stood from the two rak'ahs, he raised his hands, and he attributed that to the Prophet.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) in prayer, stating that it is only done at the first takbir (takbir tahrimah) and not at any other point – not when rising from ruku nor when standing for the second rak'ah. The author presents two hadith as evidence: first, the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah, in which the Prophet rebuked companions for raising their hands excessively, commanding stillness in prayer. This indicates that frequent hand-raising is contrary to the required tranquility. Second, a hadith from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud reported through 'Alqamah, stating that the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and 'Umar only raised their hands at the first takbir. The author then notes the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who prescribes raising hands also at the start of the second rak'ah. The Shafi'i evidence is the hadith of Nafi' that Ibn 'Umar raised hands when standing from the first two rak'ahs and attributed it to the Prophet. The author does not provide a specific rebuttal here, but the earlier evidence and the principle of tranquility serve as the Hanafi response.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer; specifically at the takbir.
تکبیر اولی (takbir ula): The first takbir at the start of prayer (takbir al-tahrimah).
سکون (sukoon): Tranquility and stillness required in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Sitting Position for the First Tashahhud (Iftiraash)
Ruling on iftiraash (sitting on left foot) during the first tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the sitting position (iftiraash) in the first tashahhud and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
For the first tashahhud, sit on your left foot with right foot erect — iftiraash is sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine a concise passage from a Hanafi fiqh text that specifies the sitting posture (iftiraash) during the first tashahhud after the second rak'ah. The ruling is supported by a hadith from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, which describes the Prophet's practice. Understanding this ruling helps ensure one's prayer follows the sunnah in posture, an often-overlooked aspect of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on and what the hukm level is. The passage states that when raising the head from the second prostration in the second rak'ah, one should spread the left foot and sit. This is the iftiraash posture.
Hukm level is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi. Identify the source (Bukhari) and the specific phrase describing the sitting: 'julasa 'ala rijlihi al-yusra wa nasaba al-yumna'.
The hadith is ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but dalala is qati because the description is explicit.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling. The explicit description of the Prophet sitting on his left foot with the right erect during the two-rak'ah sitting (first tashahhud) directly establishes the posture.
The hadith also differentiates the final tashahhud (tawarruk), confirming that iftiraash is only for the first.
4
Note the distinction between first and final tashahhud
The hadith mentions two different postures: iftiraash for the first (two-rak'ah sitting) and tawarruk for the final (last rak'ah). The Hanafi school applies iftiraash to both tashahhuds, while the Shafi'i school reserves tawarruk for the final.
This distinction is important for practical application in four-rak'ah prayers.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
When performing the first tashahhud (after the second rak'ah), spread the left foot flat and sit on it, keeping the right foot erect with toes pointing toward the qibla. This is the mufta bihi position.
Omitting this sunnah does not invalidate the prayer, but it is makruh tanzihan to intentionally leave it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية في الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى فجلس. حنفیہ کے نزدیک دونوں تشہد میں دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا کرے گا اور بائیں پاؤں کو بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھے گا۔ فقال ابو حميد الساعدى فاذا جلس في الركعتين جلس على رجله اليسرى و نصب اليمني واذا جلس في الركعة الآخرة قدم رجله اليسرى ونصب الاخرى وقعد على مقعدته (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب سنۃ الجلوس في التشهد ص ۱۱۴
When he raises his head from the second prostration in the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits. According to the Hanafis, in both tashahhuds he will keep the right foot erect and spread the left foot and sit on it. Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said: "When he sits in the two rak'ahs, he sits on his left foot and erects the right foot; and when he sits in the last rak'ah, he puts forward his left foot and erects the other (right) and sits on his buttocks." (Bukhari, Bab sunnat al-julus fi al-tashahhud, p. 114).
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling for the sitting position during the first tashahhud (after the second rak'ah). The worshipper spreads his left foot flat on the floor and sits on it, while keeping the right foot upright with toes pointing toward the qibla. This is called iftiraash. The author confirms that this applies to both tashahhuds (first and second) in prayers of more than two rak'ahs. The evidence is the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, who described the Prophet's sitting in the two-rak'ah (first tashahhud) as sitting on the left foot with the right erect. The hadith also mentions that for the final tashahhud (in a four-rak'ah prayer), the sitting is different: one puts the left foot forward and sits on the buttocks (tawarruk). The passage does not elaborate further, but the distinction is clear.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftiraash): Sitting on the left foot which is spread out, with the right foot erect.
التشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (At-Tahiyyat) in prayer.

Raising Hands Only at the First Takbir: Hanafi Proofs
Hanafi ruling on hand-raising with proofs and refutation of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands in prayer and explain the proofs from hadith that support it.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school restricts hand-raising to the opening takbir, based on the Prophetic command of stillness and the consistent practice of the first three Caliphs.

This passage addresses a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: when to raise the hands during prayer. The author states the Hanafi position—hands raised only at the first takbir—and then presents two hadith proofs. The first commands stillness in prayer, implicitly discouraging extra movements. The second reports that the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar only raised hands at the first takbir. The passage then acknowledges the Shafi'i proof from Ibn Umar's practice and offers a rebuttal, affirming the Hanafi reliance on more explicit reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its scope
Locate the statement 'He will not raise his hands except at the first takbir'. This is the core Hanafi ruling. Note that it applies to all other parts of prayer, including rising from bowing and standing from tashahhud.
The ruling is presented as a negative restriction, emphasizing that only the first takbir warrants the act.
2
Examine the first proof: hadith of Jabir commanding stillness
Read the hadith: the Prophet asked why they raise hands like horses' tails and commanded stillness. This implies that repeated hand-raising disrupts the required calmness (sukun) in prayer, making it undesirable.
The hadith is from Muslim, indicating its authenticity. The command 'sukun' is seen as evidence against extra movements.
3
Examine the second proof: hadith of Ibn Mas'ud about the practice of the Prophet and Caliphs
Read the hadith: Abdullah ibn Mas'ud reports that he prayed with the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar, and they did not raise hands except at the first takbir. This provides direct precedent from the most authoritative sources.
This hadith is from Dar Qutni and Tirmidhi. The explicit negation 'lam yarfahu' is a strong textual evidence.
4
Understand the Shafi'i position and their proof
The author mentions that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hands are raised also at the beginning of the second rak'ah. Their proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar, who raised hands at that point and attributed it to the Prophet.
The Shafi'i school relies on this report as evidence for a broader application of raf‘ al-yadayn.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response and the practical difference
The Hanafi response is implicit: the proofs from Jabir and Ibn Mas'ud are more explicit and directly contradict the Shafi'i claim. The practical result (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis do not raise hands at the start of the second rak'ah, while Shafi'is do.
This difference affects congregational prayer when followers of different schools pray together.

ولا يرفع يديه الا فى التكبيرة الاولى [۲۰۳] (۳۳) فاذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية في الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى فجلس دوسری رکعت میں بسم اللہ آہستہ سے پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ قرآت سے پہلے بسم اللہ آہستہ سے پڑھنا مسنون ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال كان النبي الله يفتتح صلوته ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم (ترمذی شریف، باب من رأی الجهر بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم ص نمبر ۲۴۵) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر رکعت کو بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم سے شروع کرنا چاہئے (دار قطنی نمبر ۱۴۳ میں بھی ہے) (۲۰۲) (۳۲) ہاتھ نہیں اٹھائے گا مگر تکبیر اولی کے وقت۔ حنفیہ کے نزدیک تکبیر اولی کے علاوہ میں ہاتھ اٹھانا مسنون نہیں ہے۔ نہ رکوع سے اٹھتے وقت اور نہ دوسری رکعت شروع کرتے وقت ۔ اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر 1 میں نوٹ کے تحت گزر چکی ہے۔ دلیل یہ بھی یادر کھیں کہ کہ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر بن سمرة قال خرج علينا رسول الله الا الله فقال مالی اراکم رفعی ایدیکم كانها اذ ناب خیل شمس؟ اسكنوا في الصلوة (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب الامر بالسكون في الصلوة وانهى عن الاشارة بالید ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۴۳۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں سکون اور اطمینان مطلوب ہے۔ اور بار بار ہاتھ اٹھانے میں سکون نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے بھی رفع یدین نہیں ہونا چاہئے (۲) عـن عـلـقـمـة عـن عبد الله قال صليت مع النبي الا الله ومع ابي بكر و مع عمر فلم يرفع ايديهم الا عند التكبيرة الأولى في افتتاح الصلوة (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب ذكر التكبير ورفع الیدین الخ ص ۲۹۶ نمبر ۱۲۰ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء ان النبی ل لم يرفع الا في اول مرة ص ۵۰ نمبر ۲۵۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر اولی کے علاوہ کسی وقت بھی رفع یدین نہیں کرنا چاہئے۔ قائی امام شافعی دوسری رکعت کے شروع میں بھی رفع یدین کے قائل ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عـن نـافـع ان ابن عمر كان اذا دخل في الصلوة ... واذا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه و رفع ذلك ابن عمر الى النبي الله (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب رفع الیدین اذا قام من الرکعتین ص ۱۰۲) اس لئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک دوسری رکعت شروع کرتے وقت بھی رفع یدین ہے۔ (۲۰۳) (۳۳) پس جبکہ سر دوسری رکعت میں دوسرے سجدے سے اٹھائے تو اپنے بائیں پاؤں کو بچھائے اور اس پر بیٹھے اور دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا رکھے حنفیہ کے نزدیک دونوں تشہد میں دائیں پاؤں کو کھڑا کرے گا اور بائیں پاؤں کو بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھے گا۔
And he does not raise his hands except in the first takbir. So when he raises his head from the second prostration in the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it. In the second rak'ah he will recite Bismillah quietly. Because reciting Bismillah quietly before recitation is sunnah. There is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet used to begin his prayer with Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' (Tirmidhi). From this it is known that every rak'ah should begin with Bismillah. (202)(32) He will not raise his hands except at the first takbir. According to the Hanafis, raising hands other than the first takbir is not sunnah, neither when rising from bowing nor when beginning the second rak'ah. Its proof has already passed in note under issue #1. Also remember this proof: a hadith from Jabir ibn Samurah: 'The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be calm in prayer' (Muslim). From this hadith it is known that calmness and tranquility are required in prayer, and repeatedly raising hands does not have calmness. Therefore, raising hands should not be done. (2) From Alqamah from Abdullah: 'I prayed with the Prophet, and with Abu Bakr and with Umar, and they did not raise their hands except at the first takbir at the start of prayer' (Dar Qutni, Tirmidhi). From this hadith it is known that raising hands should not be done at any time except the first takbir. Now Imam al-Shafi'i holds that raising hands is done also at the beginning of the second rak'ah. His proof is the hadith from Nafi' that Ibn Umar used to raise his hands when entering prayer and when standing from two rak'ahs, and he attributed that to the Prophet (Bukhari). Therefore, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, there is raising of hands also when beginning the second rak'ah.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins with the Hanafi ruling that a worshipper should only raise their hands during the first takbir of prayer. The author then provides two proofs: first, the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah commanding stillness in prayer, which implies that raising hands repeatedly disrupts khushu'; second, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar only raised hands at the first takbir. The author then presents the Shafi'i position that hands are also raised when standing from the first two rak'ahs (for the third rak'ah), based on the practice of Ibn Umar. The Hanafi response is implicit: the Shafi'i proof is countered by the stronger and more explicit reports from the Companions.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf‘ al-yadayn): Raising the hands up to the ears or shoulders during prayer, specifically at the takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a worshipper raise their hands in prayer?
A) At every takbir
B) Only at the first takbir
C) When rising from bowing
D) At the beginning of each rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, hands are raised only at the first takbir, supported by explicit hadith commanding stillness and the practice of the Prophet and Caliphs.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Sitting posture in tashahhud: iftrash vs tawarruk
Hanafi rule on sitting posture with Maliki dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sitting posture in both tashahhuds, explain the Maliki objection, and identify the contested element and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hanafis sit on the left foot in both tashahhuds; Malikis switch to tawarruk in the final—a legitimate scholarly ikhtilaf.

This lesson explores a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the sitting posture during tashahhud. The Hanafi school, based on multiple hadiths, holds that the worshipper should sit on the left foot (iftrash) with the right foot upright in both the first and final sittings. The Maliki school distinguishes the final sitting, preferring tawarruk—sitting on the buttocks with both feet pushed to the right. Understanding the evidence and reasoning behind each position will deepen your appreciation of how Hanafi jurists weigh and prefer proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate what the Hanafi school prescribes for sitting in both tashahhuds.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
State the Maliki position that tawarruk is sunnah in the final tashahhud.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith evidence the Malikis cite—the report of Abu Humayd and others.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis reconcile the hadiths and why they prefer the more general hadith of Wail ibn Hujr.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: iftrash vs tawarruk in the final sitting.
