If he wants to perform qunut, he says takbir and raises his hands, then recites qunut. (49) And he does not recite qunut in any other prayer. (50) And there is no specific surah in any prayer such that reciting anything else is invalid. (51) It is disliked... 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad from his father said: Ibn Mas'ud used to raise his hands in qunut to his chest. (Sunan, chapter on raising hands in qunut, vol. 3, p. 59, no. 4867) From this narration it is understood that he will raise his hands before reciting qunut. (49) And he should not recite qunut except in witr. The hadith mentioned in issue no. 44 passed that the Prophet recited qunut in the Fajr prayer for a month, which means that this qunut was abrogated afterwards. Therefore, now qunut should not be recited in other prayers. Their evidence is this hadith: from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet recited qunut for a month then left it (a) (Abu Dawud, chapter on qunut in prayer, p. 211, no. 1445). From this hadith it is understood that after one month he left the qunut of calamity because it was abrogated. According to Imam Shafi'i, the qunut of calamity in the Fajr prayer is still sunnah. Their evidence is this hadith: from al-Bara' that the Prophet used to recite qunut in the Fajr prayer – and Ibn Mu'adh added: and in the Maghrib prayer (b) (Abu Dawud, chapter on qunut in prayer, p. 211, no. 1441). From this hadith it is understood that reciting qunut of calamity in the Fajr prayer is sunnah. Among the Hanafis as well, they act upon this, that at the time of calamity they recite qunut of calamity in the Fajr prayer.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling and an intra-madhhab dispute regarding qunut (supplication in prayer). The ruling states that qunut is only performed in the witr prayer, not in any other obligatory prayer. The proof includes a narration from Ibn Mas'ud showing he raised his hands to his chest during qunut. The commentary explains that the qunut of calamity (qunut al-nazilah) recited by the Prophet in Fajr prayer for a month was abrogated, so it is not sunnah on a regular basis. Imam Shafi'i argues that this qunut remains sunnah in Fajr (and Maghrib according to some narrations) based on hadith. However, the Hanafi response notes that the abrogation is established, though Hanafis still permit reciting qunut of calamity during times of collective distress in Fajr prayer as an exception. The practical consequence (thamarah) is that Hanafis do not recite qunut in Fajr normally, but Shafi'is do. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that qunut is only for witr, and in calamity, Fajr qunut is permissible but not regular sunnah.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in the witr prayer (and in calamity, specifically in Fajr, according to some).
قنوت نازلة (qunut al-nazilah): Supplication recited during times of collective calamity or distress.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Witr prayer
C) Maghrib prayer
D) All prayers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that regular qunut is only in witr; qunut in Fajr was abrogated, though qunut al-nazilah during calamity is permissible.

No Specific Surah Mandatory for Any Prayer
Ruling that no surah is obligatory for any specific prayer with Shafi'i dispute on Fatihah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that reciting Surah al-Fatihah is wajib and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that no specific surah is mandatory for prayer; Fatihah is wajib, not fard.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding recitation in prayer. The Hanafi view, based on the general Quranic command to recite what is easy, holds that Surah al-Fatihah is wajib but not a pillar. The Shafi'i school argues it is fard based on a specific hadith. We will analyze both proofs and understand the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that no specific surah is mandatory; recitation of Fatihah is wajib, not fard.
The Hanafi school relies on the general Quranic command.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds reciting Fatihah is fard (pillar) and the prayer is invalid without it.
Opponent's proof is the hadith 'No prayer without the Fatihah of the Book.'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith and how Shafi'is derive fard from it.
They interpret 'la' as absolute negation of validity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain the Hanafi interpretation of the same hadith: 'la' negates completeness, not validity. Also the Quranic general command takes precedence.
The Hanafi usul principle: a general command remains general until specified.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: if Fatihah is omitted, Hanafi prayer is valid but deficient; Shafi'i prayer is invalid.
This affects whether a person must repeat the prayer or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٠) وليس في شيء من الصلوة قراءة سورة بعينها لايجوز غيرها كسی نماز کے لئے کوئی متعین سورۃ نہیں ہے کہ وہی پڑھنا ضروری ہو، اس کے پڑھے بغیر نماز نہ ہوتی ہو۔ فاقرء وا ما تيسر من القرآن (آیت ٢٠ سورة المزمل ٧٣) اس آیت میں ہے کہ قرآن میں سے جو آسان ہو اس کو پڑھو۔ اس لئے کسی ایک آیت کی تعیین اس کے خلاف ہوگی۔ فانده امام شافعی کے نزدیک سورہ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا ضروری ہے اس کے بغیر نماز نہیں ہوگی۔ ان کی دلیل لا صلوة الا بـفـاتـحـة الـكـتـاب حدیث ہے۔ ہمارے یہاں یہ حدیث وجوب کے لئے ہے کہ اگر فاتحہ نہیں پڑھا تو نماز میں کمی رہ جائے گی لیکن نماز ہو جائے گی۔
(50) And there is no specific surah in any prayer such that reciting anything else is invalid. For no prayer is there a specific surah that must be recited, without which the prayer would not be valid. 'So recite whatever is easy from the Quran' (Verse 20, Surah al-Muzzammil 73). In this verse it is said: recite what is easy from the Quran. Therefore specifying one verse would be contrary to this. Then Imam Shafi'i holds that reciting Surah al-Fatihah is obligatory; without it the prayer is not valid. His evidence is the hadith 'No prayer without the Fatihah of the Book'. In our view, this hadith indicates wajib (obligatory) such that if one does not recite Fatihah, the prayer will be deficient but valid.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage states a ruling and an inter-madhhab dispute. The ruling: no specific surah is mandatory for any particular prayer; one may recite any portion of the Quran. The proof is the general command in the Quran (Surah al-Muzzammil, 73:20) to recite whatever is easy, which negates any specific requirement. Imam Shafi'i argues that Surah al-Fatihah is obligatory (fard) for every rak'ah, citing the hadith 'No prayer (is valid) without the Fatihah of the Book'. The Hanafi response: they interpret the hadith as establishing wujub (obligatory, but not to the extent of invalidating the prayer if omitted) – missing Fatihah makes the prayer deficient but still valid. The Hanafi position distinguishes between fard and wajib: reciting Fatihah is wajib, not fard. Thus the practical consequence: if a Hanafi omits Fatihah, the prayer is still valid (though sinful); for Shafi'is, it is invalid.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): A religious obligation established by decisive evidence (qat'i); omission invalidates the act.
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by speculative evidence (zanni); omission is sinful but act remains valid (requires compensation if intentional).
لا صلاة إلا بفاتحة الكتاب (La salata illa bi fatihati al-kitab): Hadith: 'No prayer without the Fatihah of the Book' – used by Shafi'i as proof that Fatihah is fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling if a person omits Surah al-Fatihah in a fard prayer?
A) Prayer invalid
B) Prayer valid but deficient, requiring sajdah al-sahw if forgetful
C) Prayer valid and complete
D) Prayer must be repeated

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reciting Surah al-Fatihah is wajib, not fard; omission does not invalidate the prayer but renders it deficient.

Dislike of Confining a Specific Surah to a Prayer
Ruling on the dislike of making a specific surah exclusive for a particular prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on permanently confining a specific surah to a prayer and distinguish between makruh confinement and permissible frequent recitation.

Core Idea
Making a specific surah exclusive to a prayer is makruh; varying recitation preserves the equal dignity of all surahs.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling about recitation in salah. While it is common to develop habits in worship, the Hanafi school warns against permanently assigning a particular surah to a specific prayer. This ruling protects the reverence due to every verse of the Qur'an. Let's explore the reasoning and the exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of confining a prayer to a specific surah permanently, such that one recites only that surah and nothing else. The ruling: this is makruh (disliked).
The term 'makruh' here is likely makruh tanzihi (near permissible), as it concerns a mere preference.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is it makruh? Because it diminishes the importance of other surahs. All surahs are equally the Divine speech of Allah, so no single surah should be permanently elevated above others in a specific prayer.
The reasoning is based on the principle of equality of all surahs in terms of dignity.
3
Recognize the exception
The text permits frequently reciting a particular surah in a prayer for the purpose of acquiring virtue or following the Sunnah, provided that one does not make it exclusive and occasionally recites other surahs.
The key condition: occasional variation. This prevents the practice from implying obligation or superiority.
4
Note the Prophetic example
The Prophet ﷺ would often recite 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' and 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' in witr. This shows that frequent recitation itself is not makruh; only exclusive confinement is.
The Sunnah of the Prophet provides a model for permissible frequent recitation without exclusivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥١) ويكره الرحمن بن الاسود عن ابيه قال كان ابن مسعود يرفع يديه في القنوت الى ثدييه (سنن، باب رفع الیدین في القنوت، ج ثالث، ص ٥٩ نمبر ٤٨٦٧) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قنوت پڑھنے سے پہلے ہاتھ اٹھائے گا۔ (٥١) اور مکروہ ہے کہ کسی نماز کے لئے کسی متعین سورۃ کو خاص کرے کہ اس میں اس کے علاوہ پڑھے ہی نہیں یہ مکروہ ہے۔ اس کی وجہ سے دوسری سورۃ کی اہمیت کم ہو جائے گی۔ حالانکہ تمام سورتوں کی اہمیت برابر ہے۔ اس لئے کسی نماز کے لئے کسی سورۃ کو ہمیشہ کے لئے متعین کر لینا مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ فضیلت حاصل کرنے کے لئے کسی سورۃ کو کسی نماز میں اکثر و بیشتر پڑھے تو جائز ہے۔ بشرطیکہ کبھی کبھار دوسری سورتوں کو بھی پڑھ لے۔ جیسے حضور وتر میں اکثر سیج اسم قل یا ایھا الکافرون اور قل ھو اللہ احد پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ اس طرح سنت پر عمل کرنے کے لئے یا برکت کے لئے کسی سورۃ کو اکثر و بیشتر پڑھے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
(51) And it is disliked... 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad from his father said: Ibn Mas'ud used to raise his hands in qunut to his chest. (Sunan, chapter on raising hands in qunut, vol. 3, p. 59, no. 4867) From this narration it is understood that he will raise his hands before reciting qunut. (51) And it is disliked that one makes a specific surah exclusive for a prayer, such that he recites only that and nothing else – this is disliked. Because this would diminish the importance of other surahs, while all surahs are equally important. Therefore, it is disliked to permanently assign a specific surah for a prayer. However, it is permissible to recite a particular surah more frequently in a prayer to gain virtue, provided that sometimes he also recites other surahs. For example, the Prophet would often recite 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' and 'Qul huwa Allahu ahad' in witr. Thus, if one recites a surah frequently to follow the Sunnah or to seek blessing, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on a disliked practice. The ruling: it is makruh tanzihi (or possibly makruh tahrimi depending on intent) to permanently confine one's recitation in a particular prayer to a specific surah, such that one never recites anything else. The reason is that this implies a lesser rank for other surahs, whereas all surahs are of equal dignity as Divine speech. However, it is not disliked to frequently recite a surah in a certain prayer, provided that one occasionally varies with other surahs to avoid the impression of obligation. The example of the Prophet frequently reciting specific surahs in witr is cited. Therefore, there is a clear distinction between habitual confinement (makruh) and supererogatory preference (permissible).

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): A disliked action; if done with persistence, it may become sinful; not absolutely forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on making it a habit to recite only Surah al-Ikhlas in the second rak'ah of every Fajr prayer?
A) Wajib, because it is a strong sunnah
B) Permissible, as long as one sometimes recites other surahs
C) Makruh, if done exclusively and permanently
D) Haram, because it shows preference

Key Takeaway
It is makruh to permanently confine a prayer to a specific surah; one should vary recitation to maintain the equal reverence of all surahs.

Minimum Recitation in Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum Quran recitation in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum recitation required for a valid Hanafi prayer according to the mufta bihi view, and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires three short verses or one long verse — not any single verse.

The minimum amount of Quranic recitation required in prayer is a significant issue because it directly affects the validity of every prayer. Within the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), held differing views. This lesson examines the dispute, the evidence each side used, and the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify what Imam Abu Hanifa considered the minimum recitation for a valid prayer. He held that any single verse that is called Quran suffices, even if it is very short (e.g., just a few words).
This is the minority view within the Hanafi school on this issue.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position
State the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the minimum is three short verses or one long verse (e.g., Ayat al-Kursi). Less than that does not fulfill the requirement.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.
3
Analyze the evidence of each side
Examine the primary proof: the Quranic verse 'Faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (73:20). Abu Hanifa argued that the command applies to any part called Quran. The Sahibayn argued that customarily, a person reciting only one short phrase is not considered to be reciting Quran.
Both sides derived their positions from the same text, but differed in their interpretation of 'ma tayassara' (whatever is easy).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Consider a concrete case: a person recites only the phrase 'al-Rahman' in prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is valid. According to the Sahibayn, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This shows the importance of knowing the relied-upon position.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and its basis
Recognize that later Hanafi authorities al-Haskafi and Ibn Abidin preferred the Sahibayn's view as more cautious and consistent with custom. Therefore, the operative ruling for fatwa is three short verses or one long verse.
This is a standard example of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٥٢) وادنى ما يجزى من القراءة في الصلوة ما يتناوله اسم القرآن عند ابي حنيفة وقال ايو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يجوز اقل من ثلث آيات قصار اوآية طويلة. كم سے كم قرآت جو نماز میں کافی ہے اتنا ہے جس کو قرآن کا نام شامل ہو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ تین چھوٹی آیتیں یا ایک لمبی آیت اس سے کم جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اتنا پڑھنے سے نماز ہو جائے گی جس کو قرآن کہتے ہیں۔ اور ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ ایک آیت کی اہمیت ہے اور اس کو قرآن کہتے ہیں اس لئے ایک آیت نماز میں پڑھ دے تو چاہے وہ چھوٹی ہی آیت ہو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ فاقرء وا ما تيسر من القرآن کہا ہے۔ تو کم سے کم جتنی آیت کو قرآن کہا جاتا ہے اتنا پڑھنا کافی ہوگا۔ اور وہ ایک آیت ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک چھوٹی آیت مثلا صرف الرحمن يا صرف علم القرآن آیت تو ہے لیکن اس کے پڑھنے والے کو قرآن کا پڑھنے والا نہیں کہتے ۔ اس لئے ایک آیت لمبی ہو یا تین آیتیں چھوٹی ہوں جس کے پڑھنے والے کو قرآن کا پڑھنے والا کہتے ہیں اس کے پڑھنے سے نماز ہوگی۔ اس سے کم پڑھے گا تو قرآت نہیں ہوگی اور اس کی وجہ سے نماز بھی نہیں ہوگی۔
(52) And the minimum that suffices for recitation in prayer is that which falls under the name of 'Quran' according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: Less than three short verses or one long verse is not permissible. The minimum recitation sufficient in prayer is that which is included in the name 'Quran' according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: Three short verses or one long verse; less than that is not permissible. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, prayer will be valid by reciting that which is called 'Quran'. And we see that a single verse has importance and is called 'Quran'. Therefore, if one recites one verse in prayer, even if it is short, the prayer will be valid, because Allah says 'So recite whatever is easy from the Quran'. So the minimum that is called 'Quran' is sufficient, and that is one verse. The Sahibayn say: A single short verse, for example just 'al-Rahman' or just 'allama al-Quran', is indeed a verse, but the reciter is not called a reciter of Quran (by common usage). Therefore, either one long verse or three short verses that would collectively be considered as reciting Quran is required. If one recites less than that, it is not considered recitation, and thus the prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding the minimum amount of Quranic recitation required for the validity of prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any single verse that is considered 'Quran' suffices, even if it is very short (like a single word or few letters). His evidence is the general Quranic command to recite whatever is easy, and the fact that a verse is called Quran. The Sahibayn argue that 'urfi (customary) understanding requires enough to be considered 'recitation of Quran' in common parlance. A single short verse (e.g., 'al-Rahman' which is only part of a verse) is not sufficient; one must recite either one long verse (like Ayat al-Kursi) or three short verses that together constitute a meaningful recitation. The practical consequence: if one recites just 'al-Rahman' in prayer, according to Abu Hanifa it is sufficient; according to the Sahibayn, the prayer is invalid. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the later Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn, as it is more cautious and consistent with customary practice.

Key Terms
أدنى ما يجزئ (adna ma yujzi): The minimum amount that suffices for validity of an act
صاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two foremost companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani
آية طويلة (ayah tawilah): A long verse, e.g., Ayat al-Kursi (verse 255 of Surah al-Baqarah) which contains multiple phrases

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi madhhab, what is the minimum recitation required for a valid prayer?
A) One short verse like 'al-Rahman'
B) One long verse or three short verses
C) Surah al-Fatihah only
D) At least one full surah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi minimum recitation for prayer is three short verses or one long verse, not any single short verse.

Five Categories of Quran Recitation in Salah
Enumeration of five categories with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the five categories of Quran recitation in Salah and state the Hanafi ruling for each category.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school classifies Quran recitation in prayer into five levels with distinct legal consequences.

In Salah, the recitation of the Quran is not uniform; it has varying degrees of obligation. This passage from a classical Hanafi text outlines the five categories of recitation: from the minimum obligatory verse to the disliked practices. Understanding these categories helps a student apply the correct recitation according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories
The passage lists fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahab, and makruh. Note that each has a specific legal definition and consequence.
Fard is the minimum obligatory; wajib is required but with a different evidentiary basis; sunnah is based on the Prophet's practice; mustahab is recommended; makruh is disliked.
2
Understand the fard ruling
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one complete verse is fard. A verse of two words is acceptable; a single word or letter is disputed, with the stronger view being insufficient.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf highlights the importance of a complete verse.
3
Understand the wajib ruling
Reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah (or equivalent verses) is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers.
Omitting wajib requires sajdah al-sahw, unlike fard which invalidates the prayer.
4
Know the sunnah and mustahab recommendations
For each prayer, specific portions of the Mufassal are sunnah: long for Fajr and Zuhr, middle for Asr and Isha, short for Maghrib. Mustahab applies to the length of recitation in Fajr.
These are rewardable but not obligatory.
5
Recognize makruh practices
Several recitation patterns are makruh: reciting only Fatihah, adding only a few verses, omitting Fatihah, or reversing surah order between rak'ahs.
Makruh means disliked; avoiding it is better but not sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رت آیتوں کی قرآت کی پانچ قسمیں ہیں (١) فرض، جس سے جہاز متعلق ہے وہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک آیت تامہ ہے۔ اب اگر وہ دو کلموں پر مشتمل ہو جیسے ثم نظر تب تو جائز ہے، اور اگر صرف ایک کلمہ ہو جیسے مدهامتان یا صرف ایک حرف ہو جیسے ص ، ن ، ق تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ اصح عدم جواز ہے (٢) واجب قرآت فاتحہ اور قرآت سورۃ واجب ہیں (٣) مسنون، وہ فجر اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل ہے۔ یعنی سورہ حجرات سے سورہ بروج تک، عصر اور عشاء میں اوساط مفصل یعنی سورہ بروج سے سورہ لم یکن تک مغرب میں قصار مفصل یعنی سوره زلزال سے آخر قرآن تک (٤) مستحب، وہ فجر کی پہلی رکعت میں تمہیں آیتوں سے چالیس آیتوں تک اور دوسری رکعت میں میں سے تمہیں آیتوں تک سورہ فاتحہ کے علاوہ (٥) مکرو، وہ یہ ہے کہ صرف سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھے یا فاتحہ کے ساتھ ایک آدھ آیت ملائے یا سورۃ پڑھے اور فاتحہ نہ پڑھے یا پہلی رکعت میں ایک سورۃ پڑھے اور دوسری رکعت میں اس سے اوپر کی سورۃ پڑھے۔ یہ سب صورتیں مکروہ کی ہیں۔
Recitation of verses has five types: (1) Fard (obligatory): that which relates to [jihaz?] – according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] it is one complete verse. Now if it consists of two words, like 'thumma nazara' then it is permissible; and if it is only one word, like 'mudhammatan' or only one letter, like 'sad', 'nun', 'qaf', then there is difference among the mashayikh (scholars). The more correct view is impermissibility. (2) Wajib: recitation of Surah al-Fatihah and recitation of a surah (after Fatihah) are wajib. (3) Sunnah: in Fajr and Zuhr, the long portion of Mufassal, i.e., from Surah al-Hujurat to Surah al-Buruj; in Asr and Isha, the middle portion of Mufassal, i.e., from Surah al-Buruj to Surah Lam Yakun; in Maghrib, the short portion of Mufassal, i.e., from Surah al-Zalzalah to the end of the Quran. (4) Mustahab: in the first rak'ah of Fajr, from [tamhin?] verses to forty verses, and in the second rak'ah from [tamhin?] verses [to something] besides Surah al-Fatihah. (5) Makruh: that one recites only Surah al-Fatihah, or adds only one or two verses to Fatihah, or recites a surah without Fatihah, or recites one surah in the first rak'ah and a surah higher than it (i.e., later in the Quran order) in the second rak'ah. All these forms are makruh.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage categorizes Quranic recitation in prayer into five levels according to Hanafi fiqh. (1) Fard: the minimum obligatory recitation – according to Imam Abu Hanifa, one complete verse is fard. Brief verses like 'thumma nazara' (Surah al-Muddaththir, 74:21) are acceptable, but if it's a single word (e.g., 'mudhammatan' from Surah al-Rahman, 55:64) or a single disjointed letter (like 'ص', 'ن', 'ق'), there is scholarly dispute, with the more correct view being it is not sufficient. (2) Wajib: reciting Surah al-Fatihah and an additional surah (or equivalent verses) is wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and in all rak'ahs of other prayers. (3) Sunnah: the length of recitation (qira'ah) has recommended styles: in Fajr and Zuhr, the long 'Mufassal' surahs from al-Hujurat (49) to al-Buruj (85); in Asr and Isha, the middle Mufassal from al-Buruj (85) to Lam Yakun (al-Bayyinah, 98); in Maghrib, the short Mufassal from al-Zalzalah (99) to the end. (4) Mustahab: in Fajr, to recite from a certain amount to about forty verses in the first rak'ah and less in the second, besides Fatihah. (5) Makruh: several practices that are disliked, such as reciting only Fatihah, or adding just one or two verses, or reciting a surah without Fatihah, or reversing the order of surahs (reciting a later surah in the first rak'ah and an earlier one in the second). This categorization helps a student understand the hierarchy of recitation obligations and recommendations.

Key Terms
مفصل (Mufassal): The portion of the Quran from Surah Qaf (50) or al-Hujurat (49) to the end, divided into long, middle, and short sections
متشابه (mutashabih): Not used here. Actually the text uses 'تمہیں' which is unclear; possibly 'تین' (three) or 'دس' (ten).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is considered makruh in Quran recitation during prayer?
A) Reciting only Surah al-Fatihah
B) Reciting a long surah in Fajr
C) Reciting three short verses
D) Reciting the same surah in both rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school divides Quran recitation into five legal categories, with fard being a minimum of one complete verse and wajib including Fatihah and a surah.

Minimum Qira'ah and the Hanafi Dispute
Hanafi dispute on minimum qira'ah and classification of recitation types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the minimum qira'ah and classify recitation into its five legal categories.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa accepts any Quranic utterance; the Sahibayn require three short verses or one long verse; the school's fatwa adopts the stricter view.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the minimum amount of Quran recitation required for the validity of prayer? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed on this point. The text also introduces a five-fold classification of recitation based on legal obligation. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi school's methodology in balancing literal text (nas) with customary understanding (urf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the view of Abu Hanifa and the view of the Sahibayn on the minimum qira'ah.
Abu Hanifa: anything called Quran suffices. Sahibayn: at least three short verses or one long verse.
2
Understand the proofs
Identify the dalil for each position: Abu Hanifa relies on Quran 73:20; Sahibayn rely on customary understanding.
The imperative 'faqra'u' indicates obligation, but 'ma tayassara' is interpreted differently.
3
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, one short verse suffices; under Sahibayn, more is needed.
This affects the validity of prayer in practice.
4
Recognize the five categories
List the five types of qira'ah: fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, makruh, and their definitions.
Each category has a specific hukm level.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's view, as stated by later Hanafi scholars.
This is the cautionary approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وادنى ما يجزى من القراءة في الصلوة ما يتناوله اسم القرآن عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله لا يجوز اقل من ثلث آيات قصار اوآية طويلة. ... (ثم ذكر خمسة انواع للقراءة:) (1) فرض: جس سے جهاز متعلق ہے وہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایک آیت تامہ ہے. (2) واجب: قرآت فاتحہ اور قرآت سورۃ واجب ہیں. (3) مسنون: وہ فجر اور ظہر میں طوال مفصل ہے. (4) مستحب: وہ فجر کی پہلی رکعت میں تمہیں آیتوں سے چالیس آیتوں تک. (5) مکروہ: وہ یہ ہے کہ صرف سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھے یا فاتحہ کے ساتھ ایک آدھ آیت ملائے.
And the minimum that suffices from recitation in prayer is what is covered by the name 'Quran' according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is not permissible less than three short verses or one long verse. ... (Then he mentioned five types of recitation:) (1) Obligatory (fard): that which is connected to the [invalidity of] prayer; in the view of Imam [Abu Hanifa] it is one complete verse. (2) Necessary (wajib): recitation of Fatihah and recitation of a surah are wajib. (3) Sunnah: that is the long mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr. (4) Recommended (mustahabb): that is in the first rak'ah of Fajr from a few verses to forty verses. (5) Disliked (makruh): that is to recite only Surah al-Fatihah, or to add one or two verses to it, or to recite a surah without al-Fatihah.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the minimum amount of Quranic recitation required for the validity of prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any utterance that is conventionally called 'Quran' suffices, even a single short verse like 'ar-Rahman' or 'Allam al-Quran'. This is based on the general command in the verse 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Quran' (So recite what is easy from the Quran), and since the name 'Quran' applies to even one short verse, that much fulfills the obligation. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the mere name 'Quran' is not enough; rather, the recitation must be of such an amount that the reciter is customarily called 'a reciter of Quran'. That is achieved by at least three short verses or one long verse. A single short verse like 'ar-Rahman' is a verse, but the reciter is not called 'a reciter' by it. The author then lists five categories of recitation: fard (the minimum that saves the prayer from invalidity — one complete verse according to Abu Hanifa), wajib (Fatihah and a surah), sunnah (reciting from the mufassal surahs according to the length of the prayer), mustahabb (reciting extra verses), and makruh (reciting only Fatihah or without Fatihah, etc.). The mufta bihi (relied upon) position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, as it is more cautious and widely adopted.

Key Terms
قراءة (qira'ah): Recitation of Quran in prayer
آية قصيرة (ayah qasirah): A short verse, e.g., 'ar-Rahman' or 'Allam al-Quran'
آية طويلة (ayah tawilah): A long verse equivalent in length to three short verses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) ruling regarding the minimum amount of Quran recitation in prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) Any utterance that is called Quran suffices.
B) At least one long verse or three short verses.
C) Surah al-Fatihah is sufficient.
D) Any verse, even if one letter.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's fatwa requires a minimum of three short verses or one long verse for qira'ah in prayer, adopting the Sahibayn's cautious position.
